## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws in solids (elasticity, plasticity, and thermal effects). Typical relationships include an elastic response sigma~E(T)*epsilon, thermal-expansion-induced strain offsets, and temperature-dependent yielding/softening with nonlinear hardening in epsilon.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (Hooke with temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1*T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic response where stiffness varies with T)
- Thermal strain offset (constrained thermal expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1*(T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial with T-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1*T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3*T) * epsilon**2 (moderate nonlinearity; temperature-sensitive tangent modulus)
- Exponential stiffening/softening in strain: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1*epsilon) - 1) (nonlinear elasticity / damage-like stiffening at larger strain)
- Temperature softening factor (multiplicative): sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * exp(-c2*T) (strength decreases with T while retaining power-law strain dependence)
- Power-law hardening with additive thermal weakening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 - c2 * T (simple empirical thermo-softening trend)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type inversion (implicit compliance form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (elastic + nonlinear plastic strain; useful when data behaves as elastic then hardening)
- Elastic–plastic bilinear with temperature-dependent yield: sigma = Min((c0 + c1*T)*epsilon, (c2 + c3*T) + (c4 + c5*T)*epsilon) (piecewise elastic then linear hardening; yield shifts with T)
- Smooth yield transition (regularized elastic-plastic): sigma = (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon - c2*log(1 + exp(c3*((c0 + c1*T)*epsilon - (c4 + c5*T)))) (smooth approximation of yielding/flow onset)
- Johnson–Cook-like thermal softening without strain-rate: sigma = (c0 + c1*epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3*(T - c4))**c5 (plastic flow stress with strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Hyperbolic tangent saturation in stress: sigma = (c0 + c1*T) * tanh(c2*epsilon) (stress saturates at large strain; captures limited strength/flow plateau)
- Rational hardening law (saturating hardening): sigma = (c0 + c1*T) * (epsilon / (epsilon + c2)) (rapid initial rise then saturation; temperature scales overall level)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → use sigma = E(T)*epsilon with E(T) as (c0 + c1*T), exp(-c*T), or (1 - c*(T-c0))**n to capture thermal softening
- Thermal expansion under constraint → use an effective strain shift epsilon - c*(T-c0) so that sigma≈0 when epsilon equals thermal strain
- Elastic-to-plastic transition (yielding) → use piecewise Min/Max forms or smooth transitions via log(1+exp(k*x)) to represent a knee in sigma–epsilon
- Strain hardening at large epsilon → use power-law epsilon**n or (1 + c*epsilon)**n multipliers on a strength scale; often combined with T-dependent prefactors
- Saturation/plateau in flow stress → use tanh(c*epsilon) or epsilon/(epsilon+c) to model approaches to a limiting stress
- Nonlinear elastic stiffening/softening → use exp(c*epsilon)-1 or polynomial terms in epsilon to capture curvature before yield or in hyperelastic regimes
- Thermal weakening primarily affects yield/strength more than initial slope → model E(T) weakly varying while yield term (c0+c1*T) varies strongly in additive/multiplicative form
- High-T approach to melting/transition temperature → incorporate a normalized temperature gap (T - c0) inside (1 - c*(T-c0))**n or exp(-c*(T-c0)) to represent rapid loss of strength near a critical T

Best expression     : c0*cos(T + c1)*Abs(epsilon) + c2 + c3*epsilon**2 + c4*sin(c5 + c6*exp(T*c7 + c8*Abs(epsilon)))
Structure desc      : Additive model: a constant + quadratic polynomial in epsilon + a |epsilon|-scaled cosine in T + a nested sine-of-exponential term sin(c5 + c6*exp(c7*T + c8*|epsilon|)). T enters only inside trig/exponential, while epsilon enters via epsilon^2, |epsilon|, and inside the exponent. With c2≈95.53 and c3≈72.33 the baseline and quadratic dominate magnitude; the oscillatory parts are sizable (c0≈7.75, c4≈−99.6). Since c7≈−1.83, exp(c7*T+…) decays quickly with increasing T, so the inner exp tends toward 0 (making sin(c5 + small) ≈ sin(1.2833)), yielding an approximate simplification: 95.53 + 72.33*epsilon^2 + 7.75*cos(T−0.318)*|epsilon| − 99.62*sin(1.2833 + 1.0777*exp(−1.8268*T + 0.4969*|epsilon|)) (and for large T, the last term approaches a near-constant).

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci22)

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + epsilon*c2*sin(T - c3)
Candidate formulas: 67

GT (fixed):  
\[
72.33109007775502\,\epsilon^2 \;+\; 7.746546088077286\,\epsilon\,\sin(T-287.77390919062265)
\]
So GT has exactly two parts: a pure \(\epsilon^2\) polynomial term, plus a term linear in \(\epsilon\) times a sinusoid in \(T\) with **no other dependence** (no denominators, no exponentials, no extra constants).

Useful trig rewrite: \(\sin(T-a)=\cos(T-a-\tfrac{\pi}{2})\). So any candidate containing \(\epsilon\cos(T+\phi)\) (or \(|\epsilon|\cos(\cdot)\) under \(\epsilon\ge 0\)) can match the sinusoidal part by choosing a phase shift and amplitude.

---

### 1
Has extra constant \(c2\) and an extra nonlinear sine-of-exp term. Can set \(c2=0\) and \(c4=0\). Then it becomes \(c0\cos(T+c1)|\epsilon| + c3\epsilon^2\), which can match GT under \(\epsilon\ge 0\) with phase shift. **Potentially matchable**, but check: yes, choose \(c3=72.33109...\), \(c0=7.746546...\), and \(c1=-(287.773909...+\pi/2)\) (mod \(2\pi\)). ✅ **Matches**.

### 2
All terms share denominator \((c1\epsilon+c2)\). GT has no denominator. Only way is make denominator constant: set \(c1=0\), \(c2\neq 0\). Then expression becomes a linear combination of \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon^2\), \(\epsilon\), \(|\epsilon|\cos(T+\cdot)\), and \(\epsilon|\epsilon|\cos(\cdot)\), all scaled by constant \(1/c2\). But GT has **no \(T\epsilon\)** term and no pure \(\epsilon\) term besides the sinusoidal one. You can zero those coefficients, and also zero the \(\epsilon|\epsilon|\cos\) term. Then you can keep \(\epsilon^2\) and \(|\epsilon|\cos\). Under \(\epsilon\ge 0\), \(|\epsilon|=\epsilon\). So it can match. ✅ **Matches** (with \(c1=0\), tune others, set unwanted coefficients to 0).

### 3
Polynomial in \(\epsilon\) plus \(|\epsilon|\cos(T+c5)\) and \(\epsilon\cos(T+c5)\). GT needs only one trig term linear in \(\epsilon\). Set all linear \(\epsilon\) polynomial coefficients to 0; set either the \(|\epsilon|\cos\) or \(\epsilon\cos\) coefficient to 0 and keep the other. Under \(\epsilon\ge 0\), \(|\epsilon|\cos\) is fine. Also set \(\epsilon^2\) coefficient to 72.33109... and trig amplitude/phase to match. ✅ **Matches**.

### 4
Same denominator structure as (2) but includes \(T\epsilon^2\) and \(T\epsilon\) terms. Make denominator constant with \(c1=0\). Then must eliminate \(T\epsilon^2\) and \(T\epsilon\) by setting their coefficients 0. Remaining can reproduce \(\epsilon^2\) and \(\epsilon\cos\) as in (2). ✅ **Matches**.

### 5
Denominator again; also has additive constant \(c3\). Set \(c3=0\), set denominator constant \(c1=0\), kill \(T\epsilon^2\) term by \(c0=0\). Then keep \(\epsilon^2\) and \(|\epsilon|\cos\) terms. ✅ **Matches**.

### 6
Form: \(c0\cos(T+c1)|\epsilon| + c2 + c3\epsilon^2 + c4\sin(c5 e^{c6|\epsilon|}+c7)\). Set \(c2=0\), \(c4=0\). Then same as candidate 22-type: \(|\epsilon|\cos\) + \(\epsilon^2\). Under \(\epsilon\ge 0\) and phase shift, matches. ✅ **Matches**.

### 7
Has extra term \(c4\epsilon (T+c5)^{c6}\) which depends on \(T\) non-sinusoidally. Set \(c4=0\), \(c2=0\). Then reduces to \(|\epsilon|\cos\) + \(\epsilon^2\). ✅ **Matches**.

**GT: 72.33*epsilon² + 7.747*epsilon*sin(T - 287.77)**

Key observations about GT:
- It has an `epsilon²` term
- It has an `epsilon*sin(T + const)` term (note: sin(T - 287.77) = cos(T + phase) for appropriate phase)
- No constant offset term
- No terms with T*epsilon, exp(T), log(T), etc.

Since sin(T - c3) = -sin(c3 - T) = cos(T - c3 - π/2), and cos(T + c1) = cos(T + c1), we can write:
epsilon*sin(T - c3) = epsilon*cos(T - c3 - π/2) = epsilon*cos(T + const)

So the GT is: **c0*epsilon² + c2*epsilon*cos(T + phase)**

For epsilon ≥ 0: |epsilon| = epsilon, so epsilon*cos(T+c1)*|epsilon| = epsilon²*cos(T+c1), which is NOT the same as epsilon*cos(T+c1).

Let me carefully check: cos(T+c1)*|epsilon| with epsilon ≥ 0 gives epsilon*cos(T+c1). So `c*cos(T+c1)*|epsilon|` = `c*epsilon*cos(T+c1)` which matches the `epsilon*sin(T-c3)` term (with appropriate phase shift).

So GT = **c0*epsilon² + c2*epsilon*cos(T + phase)** where the cos term comes from rewriting sin.
